@ Embroidery Ring    | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321103 |    377 | Embroidery, Hoop, Needle_craft, Ring, Stitching | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/d3/f6/41/5c/95/Adjustment_screw_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryRemake of the classic embroidery ring with tension screwInstructionsSimply print the 3 parts. In order to assemble it you'll need two M4 hex nuts and a M4 bolt of 50mm.
Insert the bolt into the the 'adjustment screw' part and add one of the M4 nuts and tighten this. Add a little 'Loctite'to prevent the nut from loosening itself.
Insert the other M4 hex nut in the outer ring and secure it in place with a drop superglue and let it dry for a couple of minutes and you're ready to go!!  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ Eyecaps for Binoculars - fully parametrized | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321104 |    347 | binoculars, eyecaps, eye_caps, field_glasses, Minolta, Nikon, openscad, parameterized, parametric, Pentax, scad | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/02/73/12/6e/7c/eyecaps-1_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryThis "thing" generates bridged eyecaps for binoculars.   
Unfortunately, nowadays most binoculars no longer come with decent eyecaps which are connected by a flexible bridge and stay attached to the binocular strap. Instead, new binoculars are often only delivered with two simple plastic caps which get lost very quickly.  
Module eyecaps() in the included SCAD file is fully parametrized.  The main parameters of the module are used to configure:  

outer diameter of the eyepieces  
distance between the eyepieces when fully opened  
size and number of strap loops   
number and type of bridge between the eyecaps  

The example STL files are parametrized for the following binoculars:  

Minolta 7x21 (31mm eyepiece)  
Nikon Sportstar EX 8x25 (33mm eyepiece)  
Pentax DCF 9x28 (35mm eyepiece)  

For other eyepiece diameters, distances and bridge configurations just modify the SCAD file by adding your own call to module eyecaps() at the end of the file.  
Given that the eyecaps bridges need to be flexible when the binoculars are folded for storage, the material of choice for printing the eyecaps is definitely ABS.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">
 <div class="cc-licenses">

SummarySee V2 here as its a much better design 

This is a universal antenna holder. It was designed specifically with RC users in mind. The holes for the tubes are sized for 3.2mm antenna tube commonly used in the RC hobby.  
Mounting holes are for M3 bolts. Antennas feed thew the center hole which is smoothed.

@ Cooling ducts for rostock max - 25mm fan | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321205 |    542 | 25mm, cooling, cooling_duct, duct, fan, fan_duct, max, rostock, rostock_cooling, rostock_max, rostock_max_cooling_ducts_25mm, SeeMeCNC | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/4d/35/39/81/b6/cams_micro_fan_cooling_duct__preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryI couldn't find a cooling duct for the rostock max that I believed was light weight enough and provided enough air flow. so i made my own.
instructions for printing and mounting in instructions tab.
I have provided 2 variants of the ducts. The first fits the standard rostock platform that comes with the rostock from seemecnc. The second version has a longer stem. This is because I have recently upgraded to magnetic ball joints and the new platform interferes with the mounting alignment so I have extended the stem and ducting.
uses 3x 25mm fans and whatever mounting screws you have lying around.
Happy Printing :)
-Cambrian Grenier
CGD.incInstructionsPRINTING.
I found the best orientation for printing is to rotate it on the x axis by 30 degrees so it is setting on the back flat section.
That way you can print without support.
For simplicity i have included 1 .stl for each variant of 3 ducts in the correct orientation.
MOUNTING:
To mount the ducts i used 3 extra bolts and nuts that came with the printer and to mount the 25mm fans i used 4 small wood screws that fit through the fan.
Mount them between the arms using the extra holes that would be for the hot-end aluminum supports.  
Its all rather straight forward once you are looking at it :P
Happy Printing!  

Cambrian Grenier
CGD.inc

SummaryStar Citizen is a Space Sim game being developed by Chris Roberts, CIG, RSI.  
With the huge amount of forum traffic, videos, and events dealing with the upcoming game, T.I.B. and REDACTED have become very popular catchphrases within the community. Not quite Leeroy Jenkins yet, but you never know.  
This project started with attempts to make stamps of the Imperium Division Logos, but when small enough for the ink pad  they did not ink-stamp as well as I would have liked. (TIB results).  
So I redacted the logo effort and shifted focus to these instead. They came out very usable once sized correctly.  
Hope you enjoy them. Happy Printing. - DRUM outInstructionsThese are thick enough that a 20% fill is adequate.
Used ABS, so Acetone secured the handle very well.   
There is a flexible plastic available now. I have not worked with it yet, but with it being less rigid the results may be better when used as a stamp. If you try some and it works well for stamps, please leave a comment.  
Once the ink pad was generously saturated, these gave acceptable results at 2 inches (50mm) and 3 inches (80mm). Larger is always better with stamps.
Note that if you expand the stamp size the Handle.STL will also need modifying. - DRUM out  | <div class="thing-license" title="Attribution - Non-Commercial - Share Alike">

@ LeapFrog Creatr Extruder Modifications for NinjaFlex Rubber Filament | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321258 |   2350 | Creatr, flexible, Leapfrog, NinjaFlex, rubber | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/aa/e5/5e/f6/97/Pin_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryMost extruders won't print flexible filaments like NinjaFlex and you need to modify  the drive mechanism before you can print.  The creatr's extruder is basically a modified MK8 extruder, but most  of the spring loaded extruders on thingiverse won't fit a Creatr or they don't properly contain flexible filament.  I worked with engineers from NinjaFlex to modify my Creatr with a spring loaded extruder drive mechanism and it works awesome.
Printer settings:
Speed: 30 mm/s
Temperature: 220C  
See instructions tab for details
Enjoy!  
8/9/2014 - added step file for the whole assembly per user requestInstructionsPrint the following parts if you have a single extruder:
1) Pin
2) Arm
3) Base Plate
Print the following parts if you have a dual extruder
1) Pin (2)
2) Arm
3) Base Plate
4) Mirrored Arm
5) Mirrored Base Plate
Remove the front plate and fans from your extruder assembly. Then remove your Motor with the two screws located on the cold end bar at the bottom of the motor.  Also removed the fixed bearing plate and spacer plate behind it.  Remove the drive gear pulley and replace with a 1.75mm filament pulley (see below where to order).  The drive pulley that comes with the creatr is designed for 3mm and won't squeeze the filament enough to properly drive it into the extruder.
You need to file/sand/drill the printed parts to make sure they fit and slide together.  My prints required the hole on the base plate to be drilled out so the pin could spin freely. Be careful to not drill all the way through the parts.  I also had to file down the cut out for the drive gear pulley so it could spin without dragging on pulley.  Make sure you don't remove the bump that is located in the center of the pulley hobbled area.  This is critical for keeping the filament from being sucked into the plastic part and jamming the extruder.  The arm needs to be tapped with an M4 thread to accept the bearing screw.  I also had to drill out the Arm to make clearance for the bearing screw head.  Try to make this hole tight around the screw head.
Reassembly the extruder with the new printed parts.  The spacer plate and fixed bearing plate are not needed, but you need to remove the bearing, washers, and screw to install them on the arm. Remember to replace the drive gear pulley with a new one for 1.75mm filament.
You need to buy the following parts:
1)  Spring: McMaster Carr 9657K306
http://www.mcmaster.com/#9657k306/=ru23qy
2)  1.75mm drive gear pulley:  Ultibots
http://www.ultibots.com/micro-extruder-drive-gear-1-75mm-filament/
I also recommend checking out Ninjaflex's site for tips on printing:
http://www.fennerdrives.com/default.aspx?node=ninjaflexfaq&    | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">
 <div class="cc-licenses">

SummaryI have a Celestron 5SE telescope, which has a StarSense accessory fitted. This meant that there was no room to fit a finder scope to the telescope. I don't really like the red dot finder that came with the scope, but have a 9 x 50 right angled finder scope spare.   
Its quite a nice fit and sits under the StarSense mounting shoe.  
It will also work if you want to add a different finder scope to the original red dot finder, but I cannot guarantee it will be rigid enough.  
I have added an STL to adapt the Celestron Red dot finder to fit my finder scope adaptor and any Skywatcher finder scope shoe.  InstructionsI printed it at .2mm layer height, with 10% infill.  
You will need a 3mm dia bolt and nut. This is to tighten the finder scope to the holder, a bit like the real accessory shoe. Motor and screw diameter are customizable.InstructionsParameter Descriptions:  
/ [Global] /
screw_diameter_scale - Global scale for screw diameter.
tube_diameter_scale - Global scale for tube diameter.  
/ [Motor] /
motor_angle - Rotate motor screw holes around center.
motor_diameter - Motor diameter
motor_screw_diameter - Diameter of motor screw holes.
motor_screwcap_diameter - Diameter of motor screw caps.
motor_shaft_diameter - Motor shaft diameter.
motor_hole_dist_1 - Distance of motor holes
motor_hole_dist_2 - Distance of motor holes  
/ [Tube] /
tube_diameter - Tube diameter
tube_offset - Increases the distance of the motor hole from the motor.
tube_wall - Wall thickness around the tube hole.
tube_overlapping - Set the length of the tube hole.  
/ [Servo] /
servo_diameter - Diameter of the hole to mount the servo arm.
servo_offset - Increases the distance of the hole to the motor.
servo_wall - Wall thickness around the hole.
servo_armlength - Servo arm length. This will change the width at the end where the servo mounting holes are.
servo_length - Length of the servo mounting hole.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ PrintrProbe Z-Probe Mount for 2014 Makers Simple Kit | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321518 |    231 | 2014, 2014makers, 2014_a, Printrbot, Printrbot_, Printrbot_s, Simple, Z-probe | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/65/ad/6b/9f/db/2014-05-05_17.20.29_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryV2: Made the mounting plate thinner so that, hopefully, longer M3 screws aren't needed. Also, made the nut catch where the probe mounts a little smaller/deeper for better mounting of the probe.   
I've tried out a number of probe mounts each one with their own issues. I figured rather than sitting around waiting for someone to make one that works 100% (The one on Printrbot's website isn't even for the 2014 simple, though is says it is) I set out to grab what I liked from other designs and make my own.   
I'm am printing it right now and will provide pictures when it is complete.   
Unlike some of the other designs this one is made to be printed with no supports. The closest I got to a supportless model still had a gap on the bottom that caused all sorts of bridging issues that really weren't needed. This design has a build in socket for the top nut on the probe so there is not need to hold the top while tightening, a bigger opening at the top for the probe to come out of for easy viewing and, as stated earlier, a flattened out corner that sits flat on the bed for easier printing.   
Many thanks to Chumsize and Evannguyen whose designs served as a base to my own.  
Hopfully this one will not droop due to heat and will stay put. Crossing my fingers.Instructions2 shells
.2mm layer height
15 - 20% infill
4 for top and bottom layers at 100% fill  
No Suport needed  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ NZ Bathymetry      | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321519 |    142 | map, meshmixer, New_Zealand, ocean, Oceanography, photoshop, relief | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/20/43/8a/01/e8/nz_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryThe sea floor elevation around NZ.  
This printed well, apart from lifting at one corner. It shows the general contours well as well as the little islands and seamounts.  
After printing this I realised that this elevation is a mirror image. At some point I'll get a corrected file uploaded, until then you will need to mirror the print before printing.InstructionsI have been playing with ways to make a printable model of New Zealand locations. I've included a brief description of the workflow for anyone else who may be interested (including myself in a few months when I've forgotten how I did it).  
I got the height information from Koordinates.com (https://koordinates.com/layer/1721-new-zealand-250m-bathymetry-grid-2008/) This gave me two huge TIFF files.  
I used Photoshop CS6 to paste the two datasets together and scale them down to 15%.  Then I used the Create New 3D Object -> Mesh From Depth Map -> Plane and exported the result as an obj.  
Then I used Meshmixer: Select -> Edit -> Extrude -> z axis to create the printable.  
One problem with this method is that I have not found a way of setting the VE (vertical exaggeration) which is fine if you just want a rough representation, not so good if you want it to be faithful to the real world.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution">

@ Motor Mount Extruder | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321523 |   2927 | bowden, direct_drive, e3d, extruder, graber, groovemount, i3, prusa, wade | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/d6/d3/63/ee/e7/1.75_i3_groovemount_m3idler_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryAn extremely versatile direct-drive extruder for a nema 17 motor.  
It can be mounted as a bowden extruder (clamp included) or directly to a Wade-compatible or i3 x carriage.  
Uses m3 hardware for motor mounting and clamp, and can use either a 623 or 625 bearing - both versions are uploaded.  
Uses an mk7 drive gear, I got mine here: http://twelvepro.com/index.php?route=product/product&path=61&product_id=51 
Allows full access to the idler teeth, even while printing - with tension adjust exposed as well.  
The clamps are meant for use on a Graber i3 printer - so they use 6-32 English hardware.  I prefer to use the clamp to mount the extruder, rather than the extruder with the i3 mount built in.  
The bowden mounts are meant for use with the E3d hotend - their bowden tube pushfits have been drilled out, so the tube can pass all the way through - there is a hole for the tube to enter the extruder, and make sure that your filament is 100% guided.  
WHY another extruder?
1) it fits on a motor
2) it's modular - can adapt to wade or i3 mounts, bowden or wade
3) Minimal part count
4) Easy access to drive gear, you can even clean while printing!
5) Fully guided filament path
6) Super clamping power!
7) Tiny.InstructionsPrint WITHOUT support - all necessary supports are built-in with onionskin, and all cylinders are capped for easy printing.  
I usually use a .2mm height; the onionskin will work fine up to .3mm layer heights, but beyond that you might need to edit the scad.  
PARTS - needed for every version
3 6mm or 8mm m3 socket cap screws
1 20mm m3 screw
1 m3 nut  
PARTS - m3 idler
1 14mm m3 screw
1 m3 nut
1 623zz bearing  
Parts - m5 idler
1 14mm m5 screw
1 m5 nut
1 625zz bearing  
Parts - groovemount
2 6mm or 8mm m3 screws
2 m3 nuts  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution">

@ Kossel Clear PSU mount for under MDF board | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321551 |    120 |                      | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/62/9d/d4/90/c6/PSUholderFIXED_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryThis is a clip that was designed by my friend by Dumle29 with the dimensions fixed by me.   
PLEASE see the Instruction tab for instructions on how to use. And PLEASE READ ALL THE INSTRUCTIONS BEFORE ASSEMBLING.  
If you have any comments or concerns you can reach me through the comments here or send me a message on my thinigiverse profile.InstructionsPrint 3 of these out, remove your MDF board/heated bed from your Kossel, flip it over and tape or hold your PSU to the MDF board while you make markings for the clips.   
Position one clip on one side of the PSU and the other two on the other, and mark the holes to be drilled with a pencil. REMEMBER: MARK TWICE, DRILL ONCE. It's really easy to mess up with MDF board since it's so soft. You can drill the holes out with a 7/64" drill bit if you want a snug fit or a 1/8" bit if you don't want to thread the screws into the board.  
After you have the 6 holes drilled, flip the board over to the side that would normally be up and use a drill bit that is the size of the M3 bolts' heads. AGAIN, BE VERY CAREFUL, just tap the trigger on the drill, you just want enough to recess the head of the M3 screw, but if the drill grabs the board hard enough it will go all the way through. If you have a drill press that would work better.  
From there it's just putting M3 bolts through the board and into nuts that are recessed in the mounts. Nothing too hard.    | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ Replicator or Creator multi-spool holder | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321558 |    193 | accessories, creator, multi-spool, parts, printer_parts, replicator, spool_holder, useful | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/99/1c/a1/24/99/SpoolHolderKit_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
Summary20140508 UPDATE:  

New version 3 available in my list of items. Much improved design which prints faster and handles multiple spools much better.   

I usually bounce between several colors or materials when printing out stuff and the process of swapping out spools on my Rep2 and my Creator X is a PITA because some of the spools I get are those new, skinnier, but taller, spools that Makerware sells, or those spools that come from Flash Forge which have tiny-sized holes.  
They don't fit well on either unit. In short,  whomever designed them or approved their use should be made to walk barefoot through a room full of Legos. Twice.  
I decided I'd create a new spool holder that connects to the Flash Forge Creator X case (and a later design to fit the Replicator 2) which holds not only multiple spools, but spools of several different sizes at the same time.  
To start, I needed vertical arms on which the crossbar holding the spools rests. For this, I went to Home Depot and purchased a 4 foot piece of .75"x.75" square aluminum tubing for about $15  
http://www.homedepot.com/p/Everbilt-48-in-x-3-4-in-x-1-16-in-Aluminum-Square-Tube-40630/202183563 
I also picked up a round bar of 3/8" Aluminum bar stock (it measures almost 10mm thick) for $5 to serve as a crossbar, which will hold the spools  
http://www.homedepot.com/p/Crown-Bolt-3-8-in-x-36-in-Aluminum-Round-Rod-49380/202183519?keyword=aluminum+round+bar+stock 
From there, I grabbed a hack saw and measured the square tubing and cut it into two, 18" pieces  
Then, I went into TinkerCad and created the "seats" (the parts that attach to the Creator X case and hold the vertical bars)  
Then, I created bar end caps, which plug into the ends of the square tubing, to hold the 10mm cross bar on which the spools rest.  
From here, I started thinking about how to mount different-sized spools while maintaining low resistance so the spool spins easily.  
I came upon the idea of using a 3D printed hub for each different sized spool which has an inner diameter of 30.05mm  
to keep rolling resistance low, I went to Amazon and bought 2 packs of (10mm I.D. x 30mm O.D. x 9mm W) bearings (5 pieces in each pack) for $12 (including overnight shipping!)\  
Http://www.amazon.com/gp/product/B00JD4T4TC/ 
These bearings will be slipped onto the crossbar at equal intervals, then each will be glued into place with 1 drop of Krazy Glue (crazy, right?)  
From here, any combination of different sized spool hubs can be slipped onto the 30mm O.D. bearing casings, and the bearings allow the hub to spin freely, reducing strain on the feeder mechanism for the printer.  
Plus, it can hold 4 or 5 different spools (different-sized ones too) so I have easy loading/unloading when swapping spools, and somewhere handy to keep my open spools.  
Swapping out filament colors/types will be far easier. And, the new location directly above the extruder, means the filament has a more direct route into the extruder(s) so I don't have to use the tubes if I do not need them.  
Oh...it doesn't interfere with the 2 existing spool mount locations so now I can choose one of 6 different spools of filament to use and, it's removable if you need to move the printer around.Instructionspurchase the parts linked to in the description
print out the parts in the STL file
assemble    | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ PortaBerry Pi (Handheld Raspberry Pi Emulator) | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321624 |   9362 | gaming, Handheld, Handheld_portal_device, Pi, Portable, raspberry, Raspberry_Pi, Retro_Pie, Video_Games | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/6c/6f/f3/24/09/20140416_004730_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
Summary(Note: User BigLazyB has put together an excellent set of instructions/schematic for this project which can be found under the files page of his remix found HERE)  
Presenting the PortaBerry Pi! A Raspberry Pi powered portable emulation machine. Now you can take your retro gaming anywhere you go (so long as you have a pouch to carry this little Beast :P).   
The specs are as follows:
Processor: 512 Mb Raspberry Pi Model B
Display: 4.5" TFT Monitor
Battery: 9.6v NiMh Pack
Controls: Custom, running on Teensy 2.0  (Joystick, four action buttons, start/select, and two shoulder buttons)
Sound: 2 Mini 8 Ohm speakers running mono, or a stereo 3.5mm headphone jack
Operating system: RetroPie 
(Please see the bill of materials under 'instructions' for a detailed list)  
Here is a nice album full of detail shots. THIS album offers nice detail shots of the interior. A much larger construction album as well as a work in progress bill of materials can be found under 'instructions'. My submission here is currently a work in progress and I hope to finish the bill of material as well as offer a schematic very soon. As I stated in the instructions there was a lot of frustration involved in this project that pictures and spread sheets can't communicate. My advice would be to use what I have uploaded as inspiration for a project of your own. I hope you enjoy :)   
EDIT: A video of the unit in action can be found HERE 
P.S. I would like to give a nice shout out to Ben Heck. If you have a chance look him up on Youtube. His portable raspberry pi project (featured on this very SITE) was the inspiration for my project.InstructionsFor a detailed construction album see THIS album. A work in progress bill of materials can be found HERE. I will post a schematic as soon as I can.
The bill of material contains information on all the main components, it lacks only the smaller connectors and mounts as well as the hardware. I will add them asap.
All the parts should be ready to print without support. Please let me know if any of the files are acting weird.   
Learn from my mistakes and build your own personal gaming machine. It's a healthy mix of fun and frustrating and thanks to the Raspberry Pi and inexpensive TFT displays it can be done on a budget. I hope you all enjoy, I will update as often as I can with more resources. Thank you.   | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ The Stick, for iPhone 5/5S | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321632 |    506 | iphone, Iphone5, iphone_5, iPhone_5S, kickstand, organizer | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/88/f6/62/fa/36/P1170593_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryA kickstand and earphone-organizer for the iPhone 5/5S. It works with a "naked" iPhone 5/5S as well as with the Apple leather cover. Works in both landscape and portrait. Could work with others as well, but no promises. The large gap works OK with an iPhone 4/4S also, but it's not perfect.InstructionsThis is a fairly iPhone-specific thing, but the general idea should be easy to model for other phones/gadgets as well. The main thing to keep in mind is to make the gap angled (mine is 15 degrees) so it's more stable, especially for portrait use. The Apple-cover makes the 5/5S 9.2mm thick, if your cover is of similar thickness it should work.  
This is my 8th revision of the design, they've all been single-size up until now. I keep at least one of these in my pocket at all times, great for watching a video on the train, while eating, with someone else or on your nightstand. Takes up very little space in your pocket. :)

@ Andy Warhol's Signature | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321673 |    147 | Andy_Warhol, plastic, signature, warhol | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/cb/76/5a/9b/38/Screen_Shot_2014-05-05_at_9.01.20_PM_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryWhat does it mean for the value of art when it is possible for anyone to make a perfect copy?  
The recent recovery of works by Andy Warhol on Amiga disks, http://studioforcreativeinquiry.org/events/warhol-discovery,  let us explore this idea.  The screenshots of the 300X200 resolution images allows pixel perfect reproductions of the work.  
I've appropriated a portion of one of the works to create a 3D printable sculpture of Andy Warhol's signature. Find more details here
http://designmaketeach.com/2014/05/02/3d-printing-andy-warhol/ 
Please leave a comment or contact me on Twitter @DesignMakeTeach or on Facebook at Facebook.com/DesignMakeTeach. I love to talk with teachers, designers and makers about 3D printing, STEM and Learning by Making.  
Campbell's, 1985 by Andy Warhol found at http://studioforcreativeinquiry.org/events/warhol-discovery was used as a visual reference for this piece.

@ Slew bearing, 160x60x8mm | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321679 |    631 | ball, bearing, camera, forces, slew, star, track, tracking | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/08/6e/f8/46/21/slewa_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
Summary160mm outer diameter
60mm inner diameter
8mm thickness
Slew bearings can take forces that a roller bearing and a thrust bearing can't deal with.  Buying the balls in bulk and printing your own bearing is far more economical than getting a $160 slew bearing machined way beyond my needs.
I put this in Camera because I've seen the same bearing used in astronomy for star tracking.  I'm experimenting with using it in my robot arm project.
If you like this you may enjoy more of my wierd ideas.  The best way to follow me is on Instagram.

@ Robo3D Cable Clip for Bed | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321692 |    158 | cable_clip, robo3d, robo_3d | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/5f/c8/93/e6/9a/10262513_10152425646244901_1936301907_o_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryI did a linear rail update for my Y axis (see Thing http://www.thingiverse.com/make:70554 ) and the smaller amount of room between the new rails and the cables for the heated bed and the thermistor kept hitting the blocks which hold the LM8UU bearings... well, it finally managed to pull the wire on the thermistor enough that it broke it. So, I needed a cable clip to hold the wires... so, here's that design. This is the 3rd revision, and this is the one I'm setting on and like. It clears the bearing block easily, and holds the wires safely.  
Be cautious on placement of the clip, such that it doesn't cause interference with the housing (assuming you still have yours on your printer) It's a close fit, but it will clear if you position it carefully. I affixed mine to the bed with the same ultra copper permatex used for attaching the thermistor to the hotend, so shouldn't be a problem with it releasing from the heated bed at high temps.  
I printed mine at 200 micron, at 75% fill, in Black PLA.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ Interstellar Imperial Army - Homunculus Troop Transport | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321715 |   2783 | 28mm, 40k, Chimera, Guard, Imperial, miniature, Transport, War, Wargaming, Warhammer, warhammer_, wh40k | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/90/61/a6/3c/9e/chimera_fit_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryMetal Bauxes for your squishies. Now you have a transport that can move 10 conscripted meatshields at a time.  


uploaded heavy stubber  


rescaled turret, looks better now. - youll need to slightly rescale the canons.   


redesigned the side guns, they were too brittle when printed   


The turret mount is not incorporated into the body. This is because this chasis is used for multiple vehicles in the Interstellar Imperial Army. This makes it easier/modular for when I release the conversion kits to make the various AA/Artillery versions. Just glue the mount down to use it. Yes, that means I'm doing the other ones too.  


The body guns in the rear, are actually smaller than shown in the "fitting" model. I rescaled them, then didnt feel like updating that model. The stand alone files for the side/rear guns are in fact correct. The fitting file is just a point of reference.   

I added the front bolter/stubber  

Trying to stay in line with Games Workshop IP Policy. If any GW employee or representative wishes me to remove or alter any designs, let me know and I will comply with expediency. Below I’ve outlined how I tried to comply with their policies.
.
Overall - None of these are exact replicas. I tried to add abit of my own take on things or modification to the design. Ei kitbash it abit. Additionally, all models should just be used for painting practice. Practice messing up a paint job on a print, not your actual GW model.
.
Copyrights - I tried to make sure a “significant part” was not the same. Style, yes. Copied, no.
.
Trademark - I’ve removed all specific Trademarks. Ex: Aquila
Non-commercial - I’m making no money from this
.
Professional Distribution - I’m not a professional artist, using any of these as a portfolio advertisement. Just a hobbiest tinkering
.
Damage our brand - Not doing that. GW IP is a pretty cool universe. Hence the reason I wanted to make models that “live” in it.
.
Make it clear you’re doing it unofficial - I’m doing this UNOFFICIALLY.
.
Use trademarks appropriately - I tried to remove all trademarks
.
Derivative Works - I believe most of these models would fall under derivative works, two are three models might not, but I think most do.
.
Non-commercial recasting and 3D printing - I have not scanned any of GW’s IP.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Attribution - Non-Commercial - Share Alike">

Bringing store bought cookies to the bake sale? Play the Mom card.
Asking for just one little phone call a week? Play the Mom card.
All the power of being a Mom in one card. Wins every time. MOM Card.  

Seriously, you there with the 3D printer. Mother's day is Sunday, May 11th, 2014. Do something nice for her and not just this card, something nice. And if you are going to 3D print something you should design it yourself. It should be something thoughtful and personalized. But when you run out of time... MOM Card.

@ Bench Dogs         | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321750 |    260 |                      | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/56/66/1f/c9/68/bench_dog__3__preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryI needed some "bench dogs" for my work bench, and I decided to see if I can print some that will hold up to the pressure of my woodworking.  I also made it with 1 degree angle on the face to exert some downward pressure (in theory).  
I made a couple prints of long one, and tested them on my bench.  So far so good.  The 20% infill felt a little light but held up, and the 80% infill was solid as a rock. I added slot and holes to maybe add some spring clips to hold it in place.  However the print warped a little bit and it fits snugly in the holes.  
These are meant for 3/4" dog holes on a woodworking workbench.  You can buy metal ones, but I would rather use plastic or wood ones in case I hit it with my hand planes.  
I made a short version that is printing now, and of course I put my name on them... because why not.  
Original inspiration was from seeing this thing: http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:320593  it made me think of doing my own.  Modeled from scratch in tinkercad.    | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ Cubecube           | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321759 |    550 | bryan_cera, cad, cubecube, kavi_laud, milwaukee, tactile | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/10/ea/e6/1e/3f/cubecube_cube_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryCUBECUBE  
https://www.youtube.com/watch?v=AJREy4lCCQA 
Cubecube is a tangible, tactile interface for CAD (computer-aided drafting.)  As open source design platforms continue to emerge, there is an opportunity to explore new possibilities in how we create. The Cubecube project aims to investigate the question: If there were a platform for using your hands to build three-dimensional computer models, what might it look like?  
Cubecube is open source.  Source code for firmware and software, along with hardware designs and schematics, are available for free download on the internet.  The current prototype is built completely around open-source creative platforms: its hardware is designed in Fritzing and connects with an Arduino Nano; its firmware is written in Arduino; its software is written in Processing.  Full build instructions have been published on Instructables.com, which include step-by-step instructions with photos, a bill of materials, necessary files, and useful links to anyone interested in participating in this project.  
The system behind Cubecube is simple.  Its building blocks each contain a tiny resistor, and as they are stacked in parallel over a voltage divider, a change in voltage can be read by a microcontroller.  Four analog multiplexers break the NanoÃÂ¢ÃÂÃÂs inputs out into 64 discrete channels.  Each channel, arranged into an 8x8 grid, reads a changing voltage determined by the number of cubes in the stack.  The current prototype supports up to 640 cubes.  
The Cubecube firmware and software, written by Kavinath Laud, was built in Arduino and Processing.  The Cubecube Processing app utilizes Marius WatzÃÂ¢ÃÂÃÂs Modelbuilder libraries to facilitate export of STL (stereo lithography) format files.  This makes it easy to interface directly with any 3-D printer system, and allows a user to extend CubecubeÃÂ¢ÃÂÃÂs functionality with third party CAD environments.  
The back-end of Cubecube is versatile.  While designed as a CAD interface, it can be modified for any number of hardware-interface projects or experiments.  Because it is designed with accessibility in mind, Cubecube can easily be hacked, iterated, appropriated or otherwise re-purposed.  The open source framework it was built around gives anyone the tools to make Cubecube their own.  
Cubecube makes creating 3-D computer models as simple as building with blocks.  The simplicity of its front-end allows for anyone who can grasp and stack objects the ability to engage with digital fabrication methodologies, and the accessibility of its back-end provides a starting point for further experimentation in the realm of tactile CAD interfaces.  Cubecube offers a different way of thinking about computer-aided design, and provides a strange but familiar platform for creating.InstructionsFor full build instructions, please visit:  
http://www.instructables.com/id/ETP6CQBHURHNJPU/  | <div class="thing-license" title="Attribution - Non-Commercial - Share Alike">

@ Custom Perlick Beer Tap Handles | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321785 |    679 | 38-1, 38-16, 525s, 525ss, 625, beer, beer_tap, faucet, perlick, perlick_tap, tap | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/5c/80/0b/73/5d/post-32838-13980737546342_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryAs I've had a few prototypes during the process of doing a custom commission for some Perlick tap handles, I decided to include my favourite three versions. The two 150mm tap handles will print completely support free on a Replicator 2, with the 205mm tall one needing support and different alignment. The 150mm tall ones will print standing as they are in the photo.  
These have all been modified to fit one of two Ez-Lok threaded inserts. The part numbers are 240-6-BR and 240-6-CR (These are the press fit inserts designed to fit a 3/8-16 thread as seen on the Perlick taps).  
All work is my own. Please tag me if you remix.  
The insert parts are designed to fit 75x75mm acrylic sheeting, which we use at our local brew club on the taps to write beers on with chalk pens. I think I designed them to hold up to 4mm thick acrylic. My recommendation is to print them in black.  
Attached photos are of the 150mm tap handles with inserts, which I will be using on my personal setup.  
And also, RDWHAHBInstructionsFor the shorter two, print standing upright if your machine is capable of printing at 150mm tall.  
For the bigger handle, work out the best alignment for your printer.  
Sand with wet and dry, prime with a filling primer, and paint.  
Cut acrylic sheet to 75x75mm or slightly smaller, use up to 4? mm thick.  
I'd personally recommend a contrasting colour to the printed object. Slide insert in, write with a fine chalk pen on it!  
Use an EZ-LOK threaded insert, push it in, thread it onto the tap. Adjust the tap to face forward. The inserts are designed to dig in once fully threaded on to seal in. For added security, maybe a bit of non-solvent glue around the knurling on the insert to lock it into place.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution">

@ MakerFarm Prusa i3v Improved End Stop Switch Brackets | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321810 |   1275 | MakerFarm, Prusa_i3v | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/48/30/00/34/a9/ZLimitSwitchBracket_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryThe new MakerFarm Prusa i3v printer (with the aluminum V-Slot extrusions) is solid and smooth, but the end-stops leave a little to be desired.  The Z stop requires splitting the wood and is still difficult to get aligned to engage the X idler properly.  The X stop won't move far enough to the right to use all of the glass.  The Y stop is mounted upside down so the screw in the bed engages the hinge end of the switch lever.  These all appear to be compromises to allow the zip ties to fit into the extrusion slot.  
These printed end stop mounting brackets solve all of these problems.  
The Z stop bracket mounts on the side of the extrusion to engage the bottom of the X idler cleanly.  The X stop turns the switch vertical and is notched out to fit around the interfering bolts.  And the Y stop flips the switch over to allow the sensitive end of the lever to engage the screw in the bed.  
UPDATE: I just uploaded a new version of the X end stop with a tab to zip-tie the cable.  
All of the brackets are shaped to fit the v-slot in the extrusion for correct alignment and easy adjustment.  
Use M2.5x10 or M2.5x12 screws to mount the switches to the brackets.  The holes are sized for direct tapping.  Drilling may be required, depending on how your printer is adjusted.  You can also just drill the holes out to the right size so the screws cut their own threads.  
NOTE: I also have an adjustable Z end stop that you may wish to consider:  http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:336665InstructionsMount the switches to the brackets using M2.5x10 or M2.5x12 screws.  You may need to drill out the holes to the right size for the screws to cut their own threads.  
Mount the brackets to the extrusions with the M5 screws that came with the MakerFarm kit.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Share Alike">

@ Luke Skywalker Lightsaber : 8 Component, Super easy to print, Minimal support needed | http://www.thingiverse.com/thing:321812 |  13105 | Light, Lightsaber, light_saber, Luke, luke_skywalker, Saber, Skywalker, star, Star_wars, wars | https://thingiverse-production-new.s3.amazonaws.com/renders/30/b7/e7/fa/d5/2014-05-08_19.03.49_preview_featured.jpg |                      | 
SummaryThis Lightsaber is a remake from scratch of the one I posted on Star Wars day.  The middle section has been reworked to be accurate to the one used in the movie.  If you have a small printer, this model is super easy to make.  
To minimize the support structures that would have to be sanded down in order for the lightsaber look good, this object has been broken down into 8 different components.  Some pieces have some external support still, notably the control box, but it should be easy to clean up.  
For assembly of the main body, you simply remove the supports from inside the holes, fill with a generous amount of hotglue, and stick the parts together.  Start with Part 1, and move your way up the stack.  For the control box, add hotglue and stick to the side of Part 3.  Don't worry about getting the insides of the holes completely clean, the plugs are designed 1mm shorter than the depth of the holes.  | <div class="thing-license" title="Creative Commons - Attribution - Non-Commercial">

SummaryA mould that you can print out and inject silicon sealant, latex, polyurethane, etc to make your own flexible hinges for the Flexy-Hand, Flexy-Hand 2, or other applications.
.
Due to the new additional hinges for the Flexy-Hand 2 gauntlet attachment, I have modified this mould from the original 2 half design.  
http://www.gyrobot.co.uk
http://www.facebook.com/gyrobotukInstructionsPrint as many moulds off as you wish.
For each Flexy-Hand you will need 4 of the tallest hinges and 11 of the middle height. And for the Flexy-Hand 2, you will need 2 of the lowest hinges for the gauntlet attachment.
Place tape over the lower surface to stop sealant leaking.

SummaryRoller for filament spools. Designed for 608 / 608ZZ ball bearings, the kind commonly found in skateboards, inlines and rollerskates.  
Made primarily for 20cm diameter spools, but down to about 12cm fits and it should be able to handle larger spools as well. Parametric design, easily adjustable to different dimensions.  
Has a Lego base underneath, so it can be mounted on any Lego plate to keep it in place. It is slightly offset from center, so one or both pieces can be flipped around to adjust the width finer than a "lego unit".  
It uses a Lego module (originally written by Andrew Sweet, which had do be included straight in the scad file for the customizer to work. Original (non-customizer) files available as .txt files.InstructionsParts needed:  

Two of these brackets printed  
Four 608 ball bearings (common skateboard / rollerskate / inline bearings)  
Four 25mm M8 bolts + four nuts  
Some Lego to mount it on (~10-14 units long, depending on spool size)
